Chapter One: On the Guru

Obeisance to ┼Ъr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa!

┬╣Having considered the necessary rituals with the saints

and having jointly gathered them from all the scriptures,

writing truly for the delight of the blessed Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas,

I take refuge in Lord Caitanyadeva.

DDс╣м: May ┼Ъr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa, enchanter of the god of love, reign supreme!

I take refuge in Caitanyadeva,

the master who bestows power to Brahm─Б and the others,

who mercifully descended to give devotion for himself,

and by whose grace the meaning of the subject is within oneтАЩs grasp.

I write this gloss on the Bhagavadbhaktivil─Бsa called Digdar┼Ыin─л to the best of my understanding. It explains one aspect of its meaning.

In order to succeed in the very difficult task he has set out on, the author first takes refuge in his beloved Deity who has taken the form of his grand-guru by making him his shelter. [He takes refuge] in him, the deva, the one worshipable by the world, whose form is caitanya, pure consciousness. The meaning is, тАЬIn him, who among the gods consists of nothing but consciousness.тАЭ Or else: in him, ┼Ъr─л V─Бsudeva, the deva or supreme ruler of caitanya, the mind. Or also: in the Lord of his life, the deva, the master that is his caitanya, consciousness, that is, his cause for life. I take refuge means I turn to him for refuge.

For what reason [does he take refuge]? For the sake of writing about the necessary, obligatory rituals of the blessed Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas, having considered

them together with the saints, the Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas that are devoted to Sad─Бc─Бra. And why does he write? For their delight, for their supreme happiness.

Now, how will this be possible for you, an inferior person? That he answers with the word Lord, meaning the one who is endowed with all majesty, or the one who has all worshipable qualities, such as compassion, or ┼Ъr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa, since the blessed Bh─Бgavata (1.3.28) says тАЬBut Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa is the Lord HimselfтАЭ. These [three meanings] should be connected with the three alternative explanations [of the word Caitanya], one after the other.[^FNB000001] The implied meaning is that by having recourse to such a great Lord, nothing is impossible. Moreover, by thinking тАЬI am engaged here by his power, his command or his greatness, not by my independent will or anything like thatтАЭ, the author gives up his own arrogance and so on.

And now, his own opinion: ┼Ъr─л Caitanyadeva refers to the Lord or great master (Mah─Бprabhu) well-known by that name. The meaning is that nothing is difficult for me, having taken shelter of him, who is celebrated for his compassion; rather, everything is easily accomplished.

Now, all these rites are present everywhere in the ┼Ъrutis, Smс╣Ыtis, Pur─Бс╣Зas and the ─Аgamas. What is then the need for this text? That he answers with gathered or collected from all the scriptures. The meaning is that whatever verses are found in all those different places, I will here collect and harmonise in a suitable way.

┬│The name Bhaktivil─Бsa comes from the Vil─Бsa of loving devotion (bhakti) to the lotus feet of the master of Mathur─Б. May his devotees engage themselves in it!

Another reason for the bookтАЩs being called Bhaktivil─Бsa is that it stems from the Vil─Бsa, the joy of Gop─Бla Bhaс╣нс╣нaтАЩs loving devotion towards to the lotus feet of the master of Mathur─Б, Lord ┼Ъr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa. Or else, because they are the shelter of devotion, the lotus feet of ┼Ъr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa, the Lord of the master in Mathur─Б, they are the Bhaktivil─Бsa, and this book has sprung from them. May his devotees, the bumblebees at the lotus feet of the blessed Lord of Mathur─Б, engage themselves in it, that is, study this book. In the case of the alternative reading ┼Ыobhayantu: may they beautify it with the fault-destroying practices of ceaseless listening, praising, preaching and so on. This is a specific type of humility.

тБ┤Long live the greatly devoted

blessed Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas here in the circle of Mathur─Б!

May K─Б┼Ы─лvara[^FNB000004] shine in Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣ЗaтАЩs forest,

and ┼Ъr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зad─Бsa with Lokan─Бtha![^FNB000005]

Thinking that this bookтАЩs attaining splendour will come about of its own accord by the happy residence in ┼Ъr─л Mathur─Б of those savouring devotion to the lotus feet of the Lord of ┼Ъr─л Mathur─Б and so forth, the author prays, тАЬLong live тАжтАЭ. The meaning is тАЬmay they reveal their own eminence, characterised by inciting devotion to the blessed Lord and so onтАЭ because of his[^FNB000006] generally residing there only, in the city, in the town of Mathur─Б. Further, because the word тАЬandтАЭ occurs below following the two names beginning with K (K─Б┼Ы─л┼Ыvara and Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зad─Бsa), тАЬfor a long timeтАЭ should be supplied with regard to everything following it.[^FNB000007]

Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣ЗaтАЩs forest means Vс╣Ыnd─Бvana, following the statement of the Gop─Бlat─Бpan─л Upaniс╣гad.[^FNB000008] May he enjoy himself, may he live there happily through devotion, such as hearing and chantingтАФthat is the meaning. With Lokan─Бtha means together with Lokan─Бtha; by this their particular love for each other is indicated. Similarly, it is also indicated that this book was written when these people were living in those places.

of the bathing of the Lord. The meaning is that the greatness of sounding a conch, etc., will be described also. Clothing and the following refer to offerings to the Lord after bathing Him.

┬╣тБ╡fragrance (6.291тАУ317); sandalwood paste applied with a stick of Tulas─л (6.318тАУ346); flowers (7.1тАУ231); leaves (7.232тАУ258); Tulas─л (7.259тАУ357); worship of the limbs, secondary limbs and associates (7.358тАУ386);тАж

Even though sandalwood paste applied with a stick of Tulas─л is included under fragrance, it is separately mentioned because of its special greatness. Similar cases elsewhere should be understood in the same way. Leaves means Bilvaleaves and so on. The limbs means the letters of the mantras, etc. The secondary limbs refer to the flute and so on. The associates means the cowherd boys and so on.

┬╣тБ╢incense (8.1тАУ36); lights (8.37тАУ95); food offerings (8.96тАУ196); drinks (8.197тАУ203); fire sacrifices (8.204тАУ208); offerings of tribute (8.209тАУ219); water for rinsing the mouth, etc. (8.220тАУ222); fragrances for the mouth (8.223тАУ226); divine perfumes and so on (8.227тАУ231);тАж

┬╣тБ╖regal offerings (8.232тАУ250); song and so on (8.251тАУ295); the great waving of lights (8.296тАУ308); blowing of conches, etc. (8.309тАУ314); waving of a conch filled with water (8.315тАУ326); praise (8.327тАУ358);тАж

Regal offerings refer to offerings such as that of a parasol or a chowrie. Song and so on: music and dance. Blowing of conches: previously conches were mentioned in connection with the bath, and now in connection with the great waving of lights. That is the difference. [тАж]

┬╣тБ╕obeisance (8.359тАУ392); circumambulation (8.393тАУ408); dedicating oneтАЩs work, etc. (8.409тАУ421); recitation of mantras and petitions (8.422тАУ437); begging pardon for transgressions (8.438тАУ440); various offences (8.441тАУ481); wearing offered items (8.482тАУ508);тАж

[тАж] Petitions mean prayers. Pardon for transgressions means pardon for offences. Various means various types of. Wearing offered items refers to keeping Tulas─л and so forth from the lotus feet of the Lord on oneтАЩs head.

┬╣тБ╣the water in the conch (9.1тАУ12); sacred water (9.13тАУ97); worship of Tulas─л (9.98тАУ181); its soil, etc. (9.182тАУ228); the Myrobalan tree (9.229тАУ242); the times when bathing is forbidden (9.243тАУ250); acquiring oneтАЩs livelihood (9.250тАУ286);тАж

The water in the conch refers to the conch-water which has been waved in front of the Lord. Sacred water means water that has washed the holy feet. Worship of Tulas─л is worship of Tulas─л and the Lord in a Tulas─л-grove. Its soil refers to the soil of Tulas─л, sticks of it and so on. The Myrobalan tree refers to a description of its greatness.

┬▓тБ░the all-gods ritual at midday, etc. (9.287тАУ293); ┼Ъr─Бddha (9.294тАУ320); things unofferable to Acyuta (9.321тАУ330); the fault of eating without worshipping as well as that of eating unoffered foods (9.331тАУ349); ┬▓┬╣eating offered foodstuffs (9.350тАУ411); the saints; good company (10.1тАУ293); shunning evil company (10.294тАУ301); the destination of evildoers (10.302тАУ309); the terrible effects of actions such as reviling or deriding Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas (10.310тАУ318);тАж

The all-gods ritual at midday, etc. and ┼Ъr─Бddha refer to the rules for how Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas are to perform these rituals, as the author writes about Vaiс╣гс╣Зava rituals. [тАж] Saints: devotees of the Lord. [тАж] Even though the terrible effects of actions such as reviling or deriding Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas is included within the destination of evildoers, the characteristics of offending the Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas are separately mentioned in order to encourage the giving up of this supreme wickedness.

[тАж] Duties at night refer to rituals such as offering the Lord his bed after song and dance. Dar┼Ыana: viewing the sacred image one has worshipped. Etc. refers to the means to attain the result of the worship for those lacking the means.

The Reason for Approaching a Guru

┬▓тБ╕Having by Lord Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣ЗaтАЩs mercy heard about the greatness of devotion in the company of his devotees, desiring it, one should worship a true guru.

Now, elaborating on each of the subjects previously mentioned, the author writes the rest of the book. Here, in verses28тАУ35, the reason is given for why he will later write that one should approach a guru, surrender to him, serve him, hear from him, and so on. He will also do similarly everywhere below. [тАж] The greatness: how it, that is devotion, is superior even to liberation. One should take shelter of a true guru, the most excellent guru, having the characteristics that will be given below.

рд▓рдмреНрдзреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрджреБрд░реНрд▓рднрдореН рдЗрджрдВ рдмрд╣реБрд╕рдореНрднрд╡рд╛рдиреНрддреЗ

рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдпрдореН рдЕрд░реНрдерджрдореН рдЕрдирд┐рддреНрдпрдореН рдЕрдкреАрд╣ рдзреАрд░рдГ ред

рддреВрд░реНрдгрдВ263 рдпрддреЗрдд рди рдкрддреЗрджреН264 рдЕрдиреБрдореГрддреНрдпреБ265 рдпрд╛рд╡рдиреН

рдирд┐рдГрд╢реНрд░реЗрдпрд╕рд╛рдп рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ рдЦрд▓реБ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН реерейрежрее

рд╕реНрд╡рд▓рд┐рдЦрд┐рддрдореН рдПрддрджреН рдПрд╡ рдорд╣рд╛рдкреБрд░рд╛рдгреЛрдХреНрддрдкрджреНрдпрджреНрд╡рдпреЗрди рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрдпрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдЪреЛрдХреНрддрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдпреЗ рд╢реНрд░реАрднрд╛рдЧрд╡рддрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рджрд┐рддрд╛ рд╣рд┐ рддреЗ ред рд╕реБрджреБрд░реНрдЧрдорд╕реН рддрдерд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдерд╕реН рддреЗрд╖реБ рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рджреН рд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐-

Broo

┬▓тБ╣One always experiences an unbearable multitude of misery in this world, and as scripture explains, in the next world as well. A thoughtful person should hence desire to cross over it.[^FNB000013]

Now, for those who are attached to sense-enjoyment such knowledge is certainly hard to attain. How then will there be a desire for devotion?тАФThat is true. Thinking, тАЬDesiring devotion even in order to cross the ocean of misery, one looks for a true guruтАЭ, the author writes this verse. тАЬOne hears about the succession of suffering from scriptureтАЭ: by faith in the words of the Veda even this is to be acknowledged. The meaning is that one should not doubt it. Knowing this, one should desire to cross this succession of misery. The meaning of the word hence is, тАЬI have no desire for devotion even though it is of such greatness! What a misfortune!тАЭ One does so if one is a thoughtful person, because otherwise one will be thoughtless like an animal, since one does not deliberate at all. Or else, one is foolish like a hunter or the like, by patiently enduring one pointless sorrow after the other.

This has been explained by Lord ┼Ъr─лdatta in the Eleventh Book (Bh─Бgavata Pur─Бс╣Зa 11.9.28):

┬│тБ░After many births, having attained this very rare,

impermanent, yet fruitful human life,

the wise one should here quickly strive for the highest good

as long as he, subject to death, has not yet fallen.

Sense objects are found everywhere!

What he has written himself he here now proves with two verses from the great Pur─Бс╣Зa.

For those who know the meaning of the verses of texts

like the blessed Bh─Бgavata, even a very difficult subject is revealed.[^FNB000014]

реерейрезрее

Broo

[тАж] Subject to death can also mean for whom there are unending deaths, or else, one who is afflicted by death, meaning diseases and so forth causing death and different and numerous great sufferings. Sense objects are found everywhere, even in births such as that of a dog.

The Lord himself has also said (BhP11.20.15):

┬│┬╣One who does not cross the ocean of worldly existence

with the foremost, easily attained, difficult to attain,

well-constructed boat of the human body, with the guru as pilot,

blown forward by the wind of my grace, is a killer of the self.

The Lord himself means the authorтАЩs own chosen deity, that is, ┼Ъr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa.[^FNB000015] Or else it refers to the statement, тАЬBut Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa is the Lord himselfтАЭ (BhP1.3.28). The word also means that this statement should be connected with the previous one. Later cases of this should be understood in the same way. [тАж] Foremost means the root of all results, since the human body can attain all kinds of results by performing deeds. Difficult to attain: not even by tens of millions of efforts is one able to attain it. Nevertheless, it is easily attained since it is attained unexpectedly. Well-constructed means very clever. Just by his being approached, the guru becomes its pilot or guide. By the wind of my grace: by the wind of simply remembering me. Or else, тАЬhaving made [the guru the pilot]тАЭ should be supplied here as well, because of the hundreds of inferences that the gravity of the speaker naturally causes to descend into this statement.

And this is the meaning: having made the guru pilot of this human body by simply surrendering to him, it is prompted towards good conduct by the guru, like a boat led by a pilot. Then, simply by remembrance, as if propelled forward by a favourable wind, it attains the true goal superintended by me. One who [nevertheless] does not cross [the ocean of worldliness] is indeed a killer of the self.

Broo

Approaching a Guru

In the words of Yoge┼Ыvara Prabuddha in the same book (BhP11.3.21):[^FNB000016]

┬│┬▓Therefore, one who is desirous of the ultimate good should turn to a guru who is immersed in scripture and in the higher Brahman, and sheltered in the highest peace.

Now, having described the reason [for approaching the guru], the author describes what to do in verses32тАУ35. In scripture means in the Brahman called Veda, in a fitting manner immersed, knowing its essence. Otherwise he will not be able to refute doubts. He is also immersed in the higher Brahman by direct experience. Otherwise he would not be able to transmit understanding. The characteristic of being deeply learned in the higher Brahman is that he is sheltered in the highest peace, supremely calm. Or else [the last part of the verse should be construed], sheltered (upa┼Ыama) in the higher Brahman, in ┼Ъr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa, through bhakti-yoga, that which is higher (upa) than the shelter (┼Ыama) or liberation. The meaning is that he should be the most excellent of blessed Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas by being sheltered in him through being constantly devoted to practices such as hearing and chanting.тАФOtherwise the meaning is the same.

In the words of the Lord himself (BhP11.10.5):[^FNB000017]

┬│┬│One should turn to a guru who knows me, is calm and whose self is in me.

Who knows me, beginning with understanding the greatness of my love for my devotees, etc. Whose self, mind, is in meтАФthe ka in mad-atmakam indicates that the compound is a bahuvr─лhi. The first part of this verseтАФтАЬOne devoted to me should constantly follow rules and regulationsтАЭ has not been given because it is not relevant here. Similar cases later on should be understood in the same way.

Broo

And in the Kramad─лpik─Б (4.2):

┬│тБ┤A Br─Бhmaс╣Зa who has destroyed the troops of enemies like lust,

whose limbs are faultless, possessing supreme devotion

that hankers after carrying the dust of the twin lotus feet of Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa,

who knows the pure paths of the Vedas, ┼Ъ─Бstras and ─Аgamas,

whose opinion is consistent with that of the saints, who is restrainedтАФ

to such a guide one truly desirous of knowledge

should surrender with humble body and mind.

Whose limbs are faultless means free from disease. [тАж] Knowledge means the mantra, the means to overcome the sufferings of repeated birth and death, and so on. With humble body and mind means dedicated only to the guide, the guru.

And in the ┼Ъruti (Muс╣Зс╕Нaka Upaniс╣гad 1.2.12, Ch─Бndogya Upaniс╣гad 6.14.2):

┬│тБ╡In order to understand this, one should, carrying firewood in his hands, approach only a guru who is learned in the ┼Ъruti and has faith in Brahman.

One with a preceptor understands.

тАЬHaving humble body and mindтАЭ and тАЬcarrying firewood in oneтАЩs handsтАЭ, as said in the ┼Ъruti, should be known to be the way of first approaching a guru.

The Mandatoriness of Approaching a Guru

In the hymn of the ┼Ъruti in the Tenth Book (BhP10.84.33):

┬│тБ╢Those who, controlling their senses and breaths, here struggle

to restrain the unsubdued horse of the inconsistent mind,

are simply tormented by their methods. Abandoning the feet of the guru

they are surrounded by hundreds of calamities.

O unborn one! They are like a merchant on the sea without a captain.

Broo

[тАж] Here refers to the sea of birth and death. [тАж]

And in ┼Ъruti (Kaс╣нha Upaniс╣гad 1.2.9):

┬│тБ╖For correct knowledge this dearest doctrine cannot be obtained by logic; it must be explained by another.[^FNB000018]

For superior knowledge this doctrine is the dearest since it is leads to the highest. By logic: by oneтАЩs own inference or reasoning. The meaning is that by following the means of the explanation of another, one is not lead off, will not be lead onto the wrong road.[^FNB000019]

Specific Characteristics of a Guru

In the Mantramukt─Бval─л:[^FNB000020]

┬│тБ╕Of pure descent, pure, devoted to conduct suitable for him, situated in his ─А┼Ыrama, free from anger, a knower of the Vedas and all the ┼Ъ─Бstras, ┬│тБ╣faithful and non-envious, eloquent, pleasant to behold, clean, well dressed, young, pleased by the happiness of all beings, тБ┤тБ░thoughtful, humble, accomplished, non-violent, reflective, having good qualities, determined in worship, grateful, affectionate to his disciples, тБ┤┬╣able both to punish and to bless, devoted to fire sacrifices and mantras, expert in logic and debate, pure in heart and a receptacle of mercy. A guru with such qualities is an ocean of venerability.

Having concisely stated the generic characteristics of the guru separately in verse32, the author now elaborates upon the specifics. Alternatively, having earlier described them secondarily in connection with taking shelter of a guru, he now writes primarily about them in verses38тАУ58.

Of pure descent: that his family line is pure, that is, free from faults such as loss of caste. The meaning is that he is born in a good family. Pure means

that he himself is without faults such as loss of caste. Non-violent (ahant─Б) means that he does not kill, or else [connected with the next word] that he reflects on the self (ahaс╣Гt─Б), that is, that he ponders on the truth. With good qualities refers to his having qualities such as being parentally affectionate. In worship means in worship of the Lord. Another reading [combining these two qualities] has тАЬof the one with good qualitiesтАЭ,[^FNB000021] that is, in the worship of the form of the Lord situated in Sattva-guс╣Зa or endowed with good qualities such as mercifulness. Determined means that he is determined in His worship.

The long final ─Б in the word garim─Б (venerability) should be excused as an archaic irregularity. Alternatively the ─Б should be read separately, meaning тАЬfully,тАЭ that is, that he by all means is an ocean (nidhi) of venerability (gariman). Or the words should be taken as separate: he is clearly the embodiment of both venerability (gariman) and of treasure (nidhi). In the case of the reading garim─Бmbudhi[^FNB000022] (ocean of venerability) the meaning is clear.

And in the Agastya Saс╣Гhit─Б (8.8cdтАУ11ab):

тБ┤┬▓One who worships the gods, who is calm, not desiring sense objects, who knows the inner self, who speaks on Brahman, who is learned in the meaning of the Vedas and the ┼Ъ─Бstras, тБ┤┬│who is competent to deliver and indeed to destroy, who is the best of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, who knows the essence of Yantras and mantras, a cutter of doubts, a knower of secrets, тБ┤тБ┤a performer of Pura┼Ыcaraс╣Зa, who is perfected in fire-sacrifices and mantras, a knower of ritual procedures, who is austere, truthful and a householder, is called a guru.

Speaks on Brahman means a teacher of the Vedas. Cutter of doubts means that he cuts the knot of hesitation.

helper of all the virtuous beings, тБ┤тБ╢free from desire, perfect in every way, learned in all the Vidy─Бs,[^FNB000024] a cutter of all doubts and who is not lazy, is called a guru.

The author gives this verse to say that one should disregard a guru who, even though he has all the qualities mentioned above, makes disciples just for the sake of his personal service and so on. Gain means wealth and so on. Makes disciples (┼Ыiс╣гy─Бt) means initiates, that is, makes a disciple, or else, one who desires service and so on from his disciple (┼Ыiс╣гy─Бt).[^FNB000025] The meaning is that such a person is not a guru. For what reason should he become a guru then? With regard to this, he writes one who is an ocean of mercy. The sense is that he desires the betterment of the world through his great compassion. Here the following words, beginning with completely accomplished, are to be understood as effects of this cause. Called means тАЬdeclaredтАЭ. One reading has тАЬis glorified as a guruтАЭ.[^FNB000026]

In a conversation between the Lord and N─Бrada in the N─Бrada Pa├▒car─Бtra (18.5cdтАУ9):[^FNB000027]

тБ┤тБ╖A Br─Бhmaс╣Зa who knows all the K─Бlas may initiate everyone. In the absence of such a person, o best of the twice-born, one who is peaceful, devoted to the Lord, тБ┤тБ╕pure of mind and all-knowing, a knower of the ┼Ъ─Бstra, devoted to good deeds and who has the three perfections, may be consecrated as a preceptor. тБ┤тБ╣A Kс╣гatriya may initiate Kс╣гatriyas, Vai┼Ыyas and ┼Ъ┼лdras, and in the absence of a Kс╣гatriya guru, тБ╡тБ░if there is such a Vai┼Ыya, he may in the same way always initiate both. O greatly intelligent one, similar ┼Ъ┼лdras can also be consecrated and initiate other ┼Ъ┼лdras.

Now, it has been mentioned that the guru should be a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa (1.34). What should one do in the absence of such a person? This the author explains in these four verses (47тАУ50). Who knows all K─Бlas, the five times mentioned

Broo

according to the method of the Pa├▒car─Бtra.[^FNB000028] Such a person can initiate, give the mantra and so on, to members of all the Varс╣Зas. In the absence of such a person, a Kс╣гatriya is can initiate Kс╣гatriyas and so on. O best of the twice-born, blessed N─Бrada! [тАж] All-knowing means one who knows all the rituals of initiation and so on. Who has the three perfections means that heтАФby way of Pura┼Ыcaraс╣Зa and so onтАФhas mastered the mantra, the guru and the divinity.[^FNB000029]

As preceptor means as a teacher of the mantra. After performing preliminary purification, he is consecrated by his own guru. Otherwise he will not have the eligibility for teaching. This is stated in the same book, at the end of the [description of the] consecration, after [the portion dealing with] Pura┼Ыcaraс╣Зa (17.49cdтАУ50ab): тАЬThus, having consecrated him according to the rules, he extends to him his own eligibility. Having received that, he should give the position of a guru to others too.тАЭ The meaning is as follows. He extends to him with his own eligibility means that the guru makes him eligible for teaching the mantra, and so on. He should means the disciple should.

Such a [Vai┼Ыya] means similar to a Kс╣гatriya with the characteristics given. Both means Vai┼Ыyas and ┼Ъ┼лdras, for otherwise there would be the fault of inverted order, and that will be forbidden later on (1.52). Similar means similar to the Kс╣гatriya with the above-mentioned characteristics.

And furthermore (18.17тАУ19ab):

тБ╡┬╣But when there is a famous guru of the highest Varс╣Зa in oneтАЩs own land or somewhere else, those who desire virtue should not initiate. тБ╡┬▓One who does so in his presence is ruined; that person is ruined here and in the next world. Therefore one should act as the ┼Ъ─Бstras enjoin. Kс╣гatriyas, Vai┼Ыyas and ┼Ъ┼лdras should not initiate in inverted order.

In this verse the author gives an exception to the previous verses. [тАж] He is ruined means that he loses all his fortune.

And in the Padma Pur─Бс╣Зa (6.253.26, 6.226.3):[^FNB000030]

тБ╡┬│A Br─Бhmaс╣Зa who is the best of the great Bh─Бgavatas is indeed the guru of humankind. Verily he is worshipable like Hari by all the worlds.

The best of the great Bh─Бgavatas means one who is devoted to all the Vaiс╣гс╣Зava Dharmas and who knows the greatness, etc., of the Lord. His characteristics will be explained in detail later on in connection with the characteristics of the devotees of the Lord (10.1тАУ293).

тБ╡тБ┤But a non-Vaiс╣гс╣Зava, even though the offspring of a great family, initiated into all sacrifices, and a student of a thousand branches of knowledge, cannot be a guru.

Even if someone is a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, famous for his good birth, study of the Vedas and so forth, he cannot be a guru if he is a non-Vaisnava. With this verse he states an exception to all the above cases. Another reading has тАЬeven though born in a great familyтАЭ.[^FNB000031] About this it is said in the Pa├▒car─Бtra:[^FNB000032] тАЬBy a mantra given by a non-Vaiс╣гс╣Зava one will go to hell. According to the rules one should take it again properly from a Vaiс╣гс╣Зava guruтАЭ.

The purpose of the word тАЬitiтАЭ here is mainly to distinguish the illustrative statements from elsewhere from the statements of the book itself. It is the same elsewhere below as well. Even though the word тАЬitiтАЭ should be used everywhere, at the end of each particular topic and after every illustrative statement from various scriptures, still, as every particular distinction is evident because of the identity of the topics, it is not given out of fear of enlarging the book too much.[^FNB000033]

тБ╡тБ╡Wise men call someone who has taken Viс╣гс╣Зu-initiation and who is devoted to the worship of Viс╣гс╣Зu a Vaiс╣гс╣Зava. Others are non-Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas.

Broo

The term тАЬnon-Vaiс╣гс╣ЗavaтАЭ was mentioned in the previous verse. In this verse, the author first states the general characteristics of a Vaiс╣гс╣Зava and then those of others, Non-Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas. Others means those different from Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas.

Characteristics of a Non-guru

In the Tattvas─Бgara:[^FNB000034]

тБ╡тБ╢A glutton, a procrastinator, one addicted to sense objects, fond of disputation, wicked, a talker of nonsense and a scorner of good qualities, тБ╡тБ╖hairless or very hairy, serving a despicable ─А┼Ыrama, having black teeth and lips and a foul breath: тБ╡тБ╕a preceptor with such bad qualities, attached to accepting many gifts even though a lord himself, destroys fortune.

Talks nonsense: one who speaks about things such as other peopleтАЩs sins, not fit to be uttered. Attached to accepting many gifts even though a lord, even though able to engage in charity.

Characteristics of a Disciple

In the Mantramukt─Бval─л:[^FNB000035]

тБ╡тБ╣Well-born, fortunate, humble, good-looking, truthful, well-behaved, greatly intelligent, prideless, тБ╢тБ░free from lust and anger, devoted to the feet of the guru, inclined to the gods with body, mind and words both day and night, тБ╢┬╣healthy, a conqueror of all sin, faithful, always devoted to the worship of Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, gods and ancestors, тБ╢┬▓youthful, whose all acts are regulated, and who is an abode of compassion: a disciple with characteristics such as these is eligible for initiation.

[тАж]

рдпрджреНрдпреН рдПрддреЗ рд╣реНрдпреН400 рдЙрдкрдХрд▓реНрдкреЗрд░рдиреН рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХреНрд░реЛрд╢401рднрд╛рдЬрдирд╛рдГ ред

рднрд╡рдиреНрддреАрд╣ рджрд░рд┐рджреНрд░рд╛рд╕реН рддреЗ рдкреБрддреНрд░рджрд╛рд░рд╡рд┐рд╡рд░реНрдЬрд┐рддрд╛рдГ ред

рдирд╛рд░рдХрд╛рд╢реН рдЪреИрд╡ рджреЗрд╣рд╛рдиреНрддреЗ рддрд┐рд░реНрдпрдЮреНрдЪрдГ рдкреНрд░рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ402 рееремрепрее

Broo

And in the Eleventh Book (BhP11.10.6):[^FNB000036]

тБ╢┬│He should not be proud, envious or spiteful, but rather active, selfless, firmly affectionate, undisturbed, desirous of knowing the goal and his words should not be vain.

Active means not lazy. Selfless means to not have a sense of ownership towards his wife and so on. Instead he should be firmly affectionate to the guru. Undisturbed means steady. His words should not be vain means that he does not speak uselessly.

Those to Be Rejected

In the Agastya Saс╣Гhit─Б (8.17cdтАУ23):

тБ╢тБ┤Those who are lazy, filthy, distressed, cheaters, misers, poor, diseased, angry, lusty, avaricious, тБ╢тБ╡selfish and jealous, deceitful, who speak unkindly, who have unlawfully acquired wealth, desire the wives of others, тБ╢тБ╢are enemies of the wise, ignorant but think themselves learned, who break their vows, behave in an evil way, are slanderous, mischievous, тБ╢тБ╖gluttonous, evil-minded, evil-natured and despicable: those and also other great sinners are the lowest of mankind. тБ╢тБ╕Irresistibly are they drawn towards sin, and they cannot endure the instructions of the guru. Thus, they should be rejected; they should not be made disciples.

Even if a guru accepts those who approach him, out of devotion or suffering, despite their lacking this or that virtue, those possessing vices must certainly be rejected. With this thought the author writes verses64тАУ72.

Distressed means expressing false afflictions. Lusty means attached to the sense objects. [тАж] Slanderous means that they speak about the faults of others, mischievous that they cause others pain. Those who cannot tolerate the instructions of the guru should not be made disciples, not be initiated as disciples by anyone. [тАж]

тБ╢тБ╣But those who do initiate them will be reviled by the gods, will here become poor, bereft of sons and wives, and after death they will go to hell and animal births.

Broo

Here the author describes the great sins that will accrue to a guru that accepts such persons out of greed and so on.

In the Haya┼Ы─лrс╣гa Pa├▒car─Бtra (5.1cdтАУ3ab):

тБ╖тБ░Jamini, Buddha, C─Бrv─Бka, Jina, Kapila and Gautama: these six are sceptics. тБ╖┬╣Those who live according to their doctrines are the lowest of men, also called sceptics. To them initiation should not be given.

тБ╖┬▓Observation is when the two live together for one year and thus experience the conduct and character of each other.

The two means guru and disciple. [тАж]

Observation

In the Mantramukt─Бval─л:[^FNB000037]

тБ╖┬│By living together for one year, the two can understand by each otherтАЩs nature what kind of guru or disciple they are. Not otherwise: that is certain.

And in the ┼Ъruti:[^FNB000038]

тБ╖тБ┤One should not initiate one that one has not lived together with for a year.

Also, in the S─Бrasaс╣Еgraha:[^FNB000039]

тБ╖тБ╡For a year the true guru should observe the disciple who has approached him. As the sins of the subjects fall on the king, as those of the wife on the husband, so the guru without a doubt attains the sins of the disciple.

Broo

In this verse the author gives a reason why the guru certainly should observe the disciple.

But in the Kramad─лpik─Б (4.3):

тБ╖тБ╢For three years, the wise one should with obliging speach,

earnestly and warm-heartedly please him with his riches,

even with his body, thinking about the lotus-navelled one.

Then, when the guru is pleased, he should ask for mantrainitiation.

Now, it has been established that there should be observation for one year, and then initiation. However, in the case of initiation into the most excellent Gop─Бla mantra, initiation should be given after three years of service to the guru. Giving the opinion of the knowers of this truth, the author also succinctly describes the way of serving the guru before initiation.

Him means the guru. [тАж] The three years here are a special case, as can be seen in other books: тАЬA Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should be observed for three years, a Kс╣гatriya six, a Vai┼Ыya nine and ┼Ъ┼лdras and others twelve.тАЭ Statements such as the one in the ┼Ъ─Бrad─Бtilak─Б saying тАЬOne year for a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, two for a Kс╣гatriya, three for a Vai┼Ыya and four for a ┼Ъ┼лdraтАЭ[^FNB000040] should be understood to refer to those who have already undergone excessive preliminary service.

Specific Rules for Serving the Guru

In the blessed Vy─Бsa G─лt─Б of the K┼лrma Pur─Бс╣Зa (2.14.8cdтАУ12ab):

тБ╖тБ╖One should always fetch his water pot, Ku┼Ыa grass, flowers and firewood. One should clean and anoint his limbs and dwelling. тБ╖тБ╕Never step over the bed he has used, his shoes, slippers, seat, shadow or ─Аsand─л. One should prepare his tooth-twig and so on, and dedicate oneтАЩs deeds to him.

Broo

The rules for serving the guru were explained briefly and in a general way in verse76. Elaborating on the specifics, the author now gives these two verses. [тАж] Anoint means to smear with sandalwood paste and so on. Shoes and slippers are distinguished from each other according to how they are made of leather, wood and so on. An ─Аsand─л is a tripod for carrying vessels for eating.

тБ╖тБ╣One should not take oneтАЩs leave without permission. One should be fond of the tasks that are dear or useful to the guru. One should never stretch oneтАЩs feet in his presence. тБ╕тБ░Yawning, laughing and so on, covering the neck and cracking the fingers should also always be avoided in his presence.

[тАж] Etc.: loud talk and so forth. [тАж]

And also (K┼лrma Pur─Бс╣Зa 2.14.28, 30тАУ32):[^FNB000041]

тБ╕┬╣One should always act in a favourable way towards the sons, wives and relatives of the guru, treating them like the guru himself. тБ╕┬▓One should not anoint the limbs, bathe, eat the remnants of or wash the feet of the son of the guru. тБ╕┬│If they are of the same Varс╣Зa, the wives of the guru should be worshipped like the guru himself. But if they are of a different Varс╣Зa they should be honoured simply by oneтАЩs rising up and saluting them respectfully. тБ╕тБ┤One should never inunct, bathe, anoint the limbs or arrange the hair of the wife of the guru.

One should always act favourably, that is, affectionately towards the children and so on of the guru. [тАж]. Another reading has тАЬConsidering whatever is favourable towards the guru, thus one should actтАЭ. Or else, тАЬwhatever one does should be favourableтАЭ.

The exceptions to this rule are given in verses82тАУ84. [тАж] Of a different Varс╣Зa: since Br─Бhmaс╣Зas formerly could accept wives from the Kс╣гatriya and other classes.

Even though all of this has been explained by ┼Ъr─л Vy─Бsadeva with reference to the service of the guru who teaches the Vedas, even so, in the teaching of the Veda with its branches, teaching mantras is naturally also done. Therefore there is no difference between this kind of guru and the mantra-guru.

Broo

Further, since the rules for the service are similar, this passage has been given here. That is the drift. Also elsewhere statements should be modified in a similar way.

In the words of ┼Ъr─л ┼Ъiva in the Dev─л ─Аgama:[^FNB000042]

тБ╕тБ╡Never step over or use the guruтАЩs bed, seat, palanquin, shoes, place for shoes, bathwater or shadow. тБ╕тБ╢Shun non-duality or the worship of others before the guru. Avoid initiation, teaching or lordliness before the guru.

Non-duality: statements of non-difference. Initiation: giving initiation to others.

In the words of ┼Ъr─л N─Бrada:[^FNB000043]

тБ╕тБ╖Wherever one sees the guru one should fold oneтАЩs hands and reverentially prostrate oneself like a stick on the ground, like a tree whose root has been cut. тБ╕тБ╕The disciple should never overstep the guruтАЩs words, seat, palanquin, shoes, slippers, clothing or shadow.

The difference between shoes and slippers are due to the differences between leather and wood and so on as explained above (1.78).

In the Manu Smс╣Ыti (2.199, 205):[^FNB000044]

тБ╕тБ╣One should not utter the bare name of the guru even in secret. Neither should one imitate his gait, talk or manners. тБ╣тБ░When the guru of oneтАЩs guru is present, he should be treated like the guru, and one should never address oneтАЩs own elders if not permitted by the guru.

Bare name means just the syllables of the name. Own elders means oneтАЩs father and so on.

Broo

In the N─Бrada Pa├▒car─Бtra (16.302тАУ303):

тБ╣┬╣One should not in any way or anywhere mention the name of the guru by itself. The self-restrained one should also not mention it without devotion. тБ╣┬▓Bowing and folding the hands, one should first utter Praс╣Зava, ┼Ъr─л, then the name, adding Visс╣Зup─Бda at the end.

Then how is the name to be mentioned? Here the rules are given: Oс╣Г ┼Ъr─л such-and-such Viс╣гс╣Зup─Бda, and that bowing and folding the hands. The long ─л in a├▒jal─лyutaс╕е is an archaic irregularity.

And also (6.304ab, 310cd):

тБ╣┬│One should not instruct him even by mistake, and one should not disobey his order. One should not enjoy anything not offered to the guru or belonging to him.

It is to be understood that one should also never even by mistake enjoy anything of the guruтАЩs, except by his order, since otherwise one would end up with the fault of ignoring his order. All of this should be understood to refer to the conduct of the disciple after initiation as well, since perpetual devotion to the guru should be observed. Therefore everything that has been given refers to after initiation as well.

And elsewhere:

тБ╣тБ┤When he approaches, one should walk towards him; when he leaves, one should follow. In front of the guru one should not sit on a seat or on a bed. тБ╣тБ╡Every day one should first offer all dear or delightful foodstuffs, drinks or other things to the guru and only then enjoy them oneself.

Broo

In the Viс╣гс╣Зu Dharma (тАУ):[^FNB000045]

тБ╣тБ╢Even if chastised or punished one should not be unkind to the guru. One should not disrespect his words nor behave in an unkind way. тБ╣тБ╖One who pleases the preceptor with wealth, life, deeds, mind and words goes to the supreme abode.

The Great Sin That Otherwise Will Befall Both

In the N─Бrada Pa├▒car─Бtra (7.121cdтАУ122ab):

тБ╣тБ╕Both one who improperly teaches and one who improperly hears will go to a terrible hell for eternal time.

The author here describes the great offence of giving or accepting a mantra without observation and service, etc., to the guru. Improperly means without the procedure of first observing each other, serving the guru and so on.

The DiscipleтАЩs Prayer

In the Vaiс╣гс╣Зava Tantra:[^FNB000046]

тБ╣тБ╣O guru, lord of the universe, protect me, burned by the fire of Saс╣Гs─Бra and stung by time![^FNB000047] I take shelter of you.

The author gives this verse to explain how the disciple should ask for mantra initiation after the guru has been pleased by his service.

┬╣тБ░тБ░Then thoughtful persons should accept initiation, which means depending solely upon the lotus feet of ┼Ъr─л V─Бsudeva, the crest jewel of all the gods.

[тАж] Thoughtful persons, since otherwise one would be stupid. This is the implied meaning.

Broo

The Greatness of the Lord[^FNB000048]

In the First Book (BhP1.2.23):

┬╣тБ░┬╣In connection with Sattva, Rajas and Tamas,

the qualities of Prakс╣Ыti, the one highest being here takes

the forms of Viс╣гс╣Зu, Brahm─Б and ┼Ъiva for creation and so on,

but for humans, the best will be gained from the form of Sattva.

Showing the reason [for taking shelter of the Lord], the author now writes about the greatness of Lord V─Бsudeva. Even though Brahm─Б and the other of the three are also masters, and even though they are one in essence, he declares the superiority of V─Бsudeva with this verse. [тАж] The best means auspicious results; from the form of sattva, from ┼Ъr─л V─Бsudeva.

And also (BhP1.18.21):

┬╣тБ░┬▓Who but Mukunda can in this world be called the Lord?

The water flowing from his toenail

purifies the world and becomes the worship water

presented by Brahm─Б.

Moreover is used in the sense тАЬeven though there are these three masters, stillтАжтАЭ Alternatively, it can be understood as тАЬnowтАЭ in the sense of presenting a new topic. Brahm─Б presented or offered worship water, water for Arghya-offerings, flowing, that is, that had issued from his toenail. Alternatively, even though [the Ganges water] had been abandoned by its giving up the toenail, it purifies the world along with ┼Ъiva. The mention of Brahm─Б and ┼Ъiva also indicates that they are his servants. Therefore, who indeed beside Mukunda can be called the Lord? The meaning is that this Viс╣гс╣Зu is certainly the only Master of all.

In the Tenth Book (BhP10.89.14):

┬╣тБ░┬│Hearing this, the sages were astonished and freed from their doubts. They placed the greatest faith in Viс╣гс╣Зu, from whom comes peace and fearlessness.

This: the greatness of the blessed Lord as narrated by Bhс╣Ыgu.[^FNB000049] Astonished: since Viс╣гс╣Зu was unperturbed by even such an offence. Alternatively, the word vismit─Б (astonished) should be read as avismit─Б, meaning тАЬnot astonishedтАЭ, since they thought тАЬyes, for him it was indeed natural.тАЭ [тАж]

In a conversation between Yama and a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa in the Greatness of Vai┼Ы─Бkha of the Padma Pur─Бс╣Зa (5.97.27):

┬╣тБ░тБ┤To bewilder the moving and non-moving creatures of the world,

the Pur─Бс╣Зas and ─Аgamas may prattle till the end of time of so many gods as the highest.

In truth, however, a collective investigation into the function of the scriptures

as a whole determines that the only Lord is Viс╣гс╣Зu.

Prattle is used in a derisive sense, like in verses such as тАЬLet them who know, knowтАЭ (BhP10.14.38). [тАж]

In the Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гha Pur─Бс╣Зa (17.32):[^FNB000050]

┬╣тБ░тБ╡Throwing my hands in the air, I declare the truth, the truth, and again the truth: there is no scripture higher than the Veda, and no god higher than Ke┼Ыava!

That there is no scripture higher than the Veda is mentioned as a comparison.

Broo

As it is said in the Padma Pur─Бс╣Зa (тАУ):

┬╣тБ░тБ╢When Hс╣Ыс╣г─лke┼Ыa is satisfied, an enemy becomes a friend, poison turns into medicine and what is wrong becomes right; but in the opposite situation, all of that is reversed.

And in the words of the blessed Lord in the same book (тАУ):

┬╣тБ░тБ╖Through my power, even a sinful act committed on my behalf becomes virtuous, but even virtuous acts done without respecting me will become sinful.

Therefore, it is said in a discussion between Brahm─Б and N─Бrada in the Skanda Pur─Бс╣Зa (тАУ):

┬╣тБ░тБ╕One who gives up V─Бsudeva and worships another god is like one who rejects his mother and venerates a dog-eating woman.

Having thus stated how [the Lord] is greater than all the gods such as Brahm─Б, the author now confirms through the statements of the Skanda and other Pur─Бс╣Зas the wickedness of giving him up and worshipping other divinities. [тАж]

This is also stated elsewhere:

┬╣тБ░тБ╣One who gives up V─Бsudeva and worships another god is like a fool who, rejecting nectar, drinks deadly poison.

In the Mah─Бbh─Бrata (тАУ):[^FNB000051]

┬╣┬╣тБ░One who by mistake gives up Viс╣гс╣Зu and worships someone else is one who throws away a pile of gold and wants a pile of dust. ┬╣┬╣┬╣One who disregards Viс╣гс╣Зu and takes shelter of another god is a thirsty man who turns away from the Ganges and runs after a mirage.

[тАж]

Broo

In the Pa├▒car─Бtra:

┬╣┬╣┬▓A blockhead who by mistake even once says that Viс╣гс╣Зu is equal to another, lesser god is an untouchable. An untouchable is not untouchable!

тАЬEven so, there is no sin in rejecting the Lord, since he should be seen as being equal to other gods.тАЭ In verses112тАУ114, the author describes this great offence. [тАж] The meaning is that one who does so even once is an untouchable, extremely low, but C─Бс╣Зс╕Н─Бlas and others are not.[^FNB000052]

In the Vaiс╣гс╣Зava Tantra:

┬╣┬╣┬│Fools, again, do not attain exclusive devotion to Hari, nor even those whose minds are one-pointed but who see others as equal to Viс╣гс╣Зu.

And elsewhere:

┬╣┬╣тБ┤One who sees Lord N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa as equal to divinities such as Brahm─Б or Rudr─Б will always be a heretic.

Moreover, the author gives this verse. Such as refers also to Indra and others. This is the implied meaning: ┼Ъr─л Brahm─Б and Rudra are Guс╣Зa-avat─Бras while Indra and the others are manifestations of his power. Lord N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa is the one who descends, the highest master; this is established by the scriptures. Thus, by seeing an equality between him and others, one becomes a heretic, since one disregards the scriptures.

This is also stated by Mah─Бdeva in the Bс╣Ыhatsahasran─Бma Stotra (Padma Pur─Бс╣Зa 6.71.305cdтАУ306ab): тАЬOne should not give [initiation] to a non-Vaiс╣гс╣Зava, a person affected by speculation, who has no faith in devotion, and who sees others as equal to Viс╣гс╣Зu.тАЭ At the end of the same text (Padma Pur─Бс╣Зa 6.71.319), Durg─Б says: тАЬAlas! Viс╣гс╣Зu, the master of all, higher than all the highest gods, the guru of you and others is seen by fools as their equal!тАЭ

Broo

┬╣┬╣тБ╡There is an abundance of such verses in texts like the Sahasran─Бma Stotra. Particularly those who are situated in Sattva should worship Viс╣гс╣Зu and no one else.

Such verses refer to statements concerning the greatness of the blessed Lord. Similarly, Mah─Бdeva states in the same book (Padma Pur─Бс╣Зa 6.71.97, 113cd, 116cd): тАЬThose who do not with all their hearts take shelter of Viс╣гс╣Зu, the Master of all masters, the primeval highest being, do not attain to the supreme good. With penance do I always worship, praise and meditate upon him. O P─Бrvat─л! I am worshipped by the world because of not being different from him.тАЭ

Furthermore, among the names (Padma Pur─Бс╣Зa 6.71.146, 151тАУ152ab): тАЬExclusive shelter of all gods; Only god of all gods; Shining like millions of suns; More difficult to approach than millions of Yamas; Creator of worlds with millions of Brahm─Бs; Stronger than millions of V─Бyus; Pleasing the world like millions of moons; Great master of millions of ┼Ъambhus.тАЭ And so on.

Further, at the end of the hymn, ┼Ъr─л Durg─Б says (Padma Pur─Бс╣Зa 6.71.314тАУ316ab): тАЬOh how painful it is that fools suffer even while Hari, the Lord of all, gives all happiness when known and rememberedтАФhe whom even our master, the naked ascetic Mahe┼Ыa, with matted hair and limbs smeared with ashes, always points to, as seen by the people. What god could be higher than him, the beloved of Lakс╣гm─л, MadhuтАЩs enemy?тАЭ And so on.

Seen by people means that this [┼ЪivaтАЩs honouring of Viс╣г┼Жu] is not hidden, but rather that it is visible to all the worlds. And so on means that the same thing is stated also in texts such as the Laghusahasran─Бma Stotra. There, in the beginning of the Laghusahasran─Бma Stotra (Mah─Бbh─Бrata 13.135.9тАУ10), it is stated: тАЬHe who is supreme, the great light, he who is supreme, the great austerity, he who is supreme, the great Brahman, he who is supreme, the refuge, he who is purer than the pure and more auspicious than the auspicious, the god of the gods and the imperishable father of the living entities.тАЭ And so on. And at the end (Mah─Бbh─Бrata 13.135.134): тАЬBy the power of great V─Бsudeva, heaven with its stars, the sun and the moon, space, the directions, earth and the great ocean are held in place.тАЭ

Particularly those means that while those whose minds are afflicted by Tamas and Rajas may worship someone else, those in Sattva should worship Viс╣гс╣Зu alone. This is the meaning. Hence the implied meaning is that one who worships another god is contaminated with Tamas or Rajas.

And in the words of ┼Ъiva in the Harivaс╣Г┼Ыa (3.90.8cd, 9cd):[^FNB000053]

┬╣┬╣тБ╢Since you are situated in Sattva, you should always worship Hari alone. O Br─Бhmaс╣Зas! Always recite Viс╣гс╣Зu mantras and meditate on Ke┼Ыava.

[тАж]

┬╣┬╣тБ╖When such statements of greatness are collected from everywhere, one will occur the fault of making the book too extensive. Therefore, they are given only when required.

Now, such statements concerning the greatness of the blessed Lord are a tonic for ear and heart, and they have been collected from all scriptures. More quotations should therefore be added! To this the author answers in this verse. There will arise the fault making the book too extensive or large. Therefore (tat) means тАЬfor that reasonтАЭ, or else, the word tat is an indeclinable pronoun referring to these very statements. The meaning is that then when they are required, they will be given, but not redundantly. This conveys the fact that such statements are numerous. By the use of are given in the present tense all such statements to be given further on are also indicated.

The Greatness of Vaiс╣гс╣Зava Mantras

In the ─Аgama:[^FNB000054]

^(118тАУ119)Reciting Vaiс╣гс╣Зava mantras, the kings of all blessed mantras, after receiving them from the guru, one will attain all majesty, the merit that can be had by thousands of years of great austerity, and then proceed to the supreme abode of Viс╣гс╣Зu. Those men by whom acts of merit and intense austerities have been performed for thousands of years recite Vaiс╣гс╣Зava mantras, purifying the world.

And in the Vaiс╣гс╣Зava:[^FNB000055]

┬╣┬▓тБ░Any person one sees with oneтАЩs eyes or touches with oneтАЩs foot while reciting Vaiс╣гс╣Зava mantras is immediately liberated from great fear.

┬╣┬▓┬╣The greatness of Viс╣гс╣Зu mantras is now described in detail, with the aim of enhancing the greatness of the blessed Gop─Бla mantra.

Now, having described [the greatness of Viс╣гс╣Зu mantras] in a general way, the author starts to give a specific description with this verse. [тАж] Now, later on the rules will be given for worshipping Madanagop─БlaтАЩs mantra, consisting of eighteen syllables and called тАЬInfatuating.тАЭ What then is the point of describing the greatness of other mantras? The author answers this objection by with the aim. This is the meaning: this Lord Gop─Бla is the source of all descents, as the statement тАЬBut Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa is the Lord himselfтАЭ (BhP1.3.28) confirms, and as the specifics of his manifold greatness also brings to light. Thus, by the greatness of the descents, his specific greatness alone will be established. Of course, the greatness of his mantra as well will be enhanced in a natural way. Thus, for this reason alone [the greatness of the other mantras] will be described.

There refers to among the Vaiс╣гс╣Зava Tantras.[^FNB000058] The form chanda [for chandas] is an archaic irregularity used as not to break the metre. Viс╣гс╣Зus means that they have attained the same form with Viс╣гс╣Зu. With Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs form: this is to indicate the colour, shape and so on that has not otherwise been mentioned.

There Also, That of the Twelve-Syllable Mantra

In the words of N─Бrada to Dhruva in the Fourth Book (BhP4.8.53):[^FNB000059]

┬╣┬▓тБ╡And hear from me, O prince, about this extremely secret recitation! One who reads it for seven days will see those moving in the sky.

The author first gave a general description of [the greatness of] both, and now he gives the particulars of the first. There means among the twelve- and eight-syllable mantras. O prince means o Dhruva.

In the Viс╣гс╣Зu Pur─Бс╣Зa (1.6.40):[^FNB000060]

┬╣┬▓тБ╢The sun, moon and the planets will all come and go, but those who even today meditate upon the Twelve-syllable mantra will never return.

Of the Eight-Syllable Mantra

As stated in the N─Бrada Pa├▒car─Бtra (тАУ):[^FNB000061]

┬╣┬▓тБ╖The three Vedas, their six ancillary limbs, the metres, all the gods, and whatever else is made of words, all that is contained within the Eight-syllable mantra. ┬╣┬▓тБ╕Its meaning is the essence of all Ved─Бnta, it enables one to cross the ocean of worldly existence: the Eight-syllable mantra is the refuge of those who wish never to be born again. ┬╣┬▓тБ╣Diseases, robbers and famine will never enter the place where the greatly fortunate person who has perfected the recitation of the Eight-syllable mantra is revered. ┬╣┬│тБ░Gods, demons, Gandharvas, Siddhas, Vidy─Бdharas and others all bow

to the great one who knows the Eight-syllable mantra, ┬╣┬│┬╣for Lord N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa himself appears in the perceptible form of the Eight-syllable mantra in their mouths.

[тАж] Having the form of sound, [the Lord] appears in their mouth.

In the Uttarakhaс╣Зс╕Нa of the Padma Pur─Бс╣Зa (6.226.18cdтАУ19ab):

┬╣┬│┬▓This Eight-syllable mantra should be known to fulfil all desires and remove all distress; it is auspicious, comprising all mantras, and splendid.

Auspicious: it is endowed with all splendour or success. The meaning is that it bestows auspiciousness on its practitioner. It is also naturally splendid, the very form of felicity.

In the Liс╣Еga Pur─Бс╣Зa (2.7.12cdтАУ14ab):

┬╣┬│┬│What is the use of many other mantras? What is the use of many other observances? The Namo N─Бr─Бyaс╣З─Бya mantra fulfils all desires. ┬╣┬│тБ┤O best of the twiceborn! One who therefore at all times recites Namo N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa will go to the world of Viс╣гс╣Зu together with his relatives.

In the Bhaviс╣гya Pur─Бс╣Зa (тАУ):[^FNB000062]

┬╣┬│тБ╡Of all Viс╣гс╣Зu mantras, the great Eight-syllable mantra is supreme and the remover of all sin. It is celebrated as the king.

And in a conversation between Vy─Бsa and ┼Ъuka:[^FNB000063]

┬╣┬│тБ╢O son! When recited by devotees, the Namo N─Бr─Бyaс╣З─Бya mantra fulfils all desires and awards the fruit of heaven and liberation. ^(137тАУ138)This is the highest liberation, this is known as heaven! It is the essence, extracted by Viс╣гс╣Зu from the secrets of all the Vedas for the benefit of the Vaiс╣гс╣Зavas. Previously praised by Manu, it destroys all sins and bestows all desires.

┬╣┬│тБ╣This N─Бr─Бyaс╣З─Бya Namaс╕е is truly the mantra

for destroying the terrible poison of worldly existence.

Listen, you who are inclined towards the truth, happy and detached:

most loudly will I teach you with my arms in the air:

┬╣тБ┤тБ░With my arms in the air, today I tell you the truth. O son and disciples, listen: there is no mantra higher than the Eight-syllable one!

O son means o ┼Ъuka! [тАж] Praised by Manu means that he recited it or discussed it among the people. [тАж]

This is also stated in the Garuс╕Нa Pur─Бс╣Зa (1.228.8):

┬╣тБ┤┬╣Sitting, lying down, standing or wherever: the Namo N─Бr─Бyaс╣З─Бya mantra should be oneтАЩs only shelter.

[тАж]

That of the King of Mantras, the Anuс╣гс╣нubh of ┼Ъr─л Narasiс╣Гha[^FNB000064]

In the T─Бpan─лya ┼Ъruti (Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhap┼лrvat─Бpan─л Upaniс╣гad 5.3):

┬╣тБ┤┬▓The gods spoke to Praj─Бpati: тАЬPlease tell us the fruit of the king of mantras, the Anuс╣гс╣нubh of Narasiс╣Гha!тАЭ Praj─Бpati replied: тАЬOne who constantly recites the king of mantras, the Anuс╣гс╣нubh of Narasiс╣Гha, becomes pure as the ─Аdityas, he becomes pure as fire, he becomes pure as the wind, he becomes pure as the sun, he becomes pure as the moon, he becomes pure as the truth, he becomes pure as Brahm─Б, he becomes pure as Viс╣гс╣Зu, he becomes pure as Rudra, he becomes pure as all of them.тАЭ

┬╣тБ┤┬│One hundred persons not initiated with the sacred thread are equal to one who is initiated with the sacred thread. And this is the highest abode of the one who studies the king of mantras: where the sun does not shine, where the wind does not blow, where the moon does not give out light, where the stars do not shine, where fire does not burn, where death does not enter, where no fault exists. The highest abode is eternal bliss, eternally peaceful, always auspicious, worshipped by the gods such as Brahm─Б, meditated upon by the yogis, and from where the yogins, having once gone, never return. The Greatness of the Eighteen-Syllable Mantra[^FNB000070]

In the T─Бpan─лya ┼Ъruti (Gop─Бlat─Бpan─л Upaniс╣гad 1.2тАУ8):[^FNB000071]

┬╣тБ╡тБ╖

Oс╣В. The sages asked the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa: тАЬWho is the highest god? What does death fear? By knowing what does everything become known? By what is this world turned?тАЭ

The Br─Бhmaс╣Зa replied : тАЬKс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa is indeed the highest divinity. Death fears Govinda. By knowing Gop─лjanavallabha everything becomes known. By Sv─Бh─Б is this world turned.тАЭ

They then asked him: тАЬWho is Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa? Who is this Govinda? Who is Gop─лjanavallabha? What is Sv─Бh─Б?тАЭ

The Br─Бhmaс╣Зa told them: тАЬThe destroyer of sin; the one known by the cows, earth and the Vedas, and who is their knower; the one who sets in motion the milkmaidens, the Avidy─Бkal─Бs; and his M─Бy─Б. This is the highest Brahman with its parts. One who meditates upon it, takes pleasure in it and worships it becomes immortal, becomes immortal.тАЭ

They said: тАЬWhat is its form? How does one take pleasure in it? And what is its worship? Please explain all this to us, who are eager to learn.тАЭ

The golden one said: тАЬDressed as a cowherd, having the colour of a raincloud, youthful, sheltered at a desire tree.тАЭ

[тАж] The Br─Бhmaс╣Зa means Brahm─Б, since he knows Brahman. Or else that Brahman refers to the тАЬdivinityтАЭ, following the previous statement.[^FNB000072] Destroyer of sin is the meaning of the second word [of the mantra, that is тАЬKс╣Ыс╣гс╣ЗaтАЭ]. That of the third [тАЬGovindaтАЭ] is the the one who is known among the cowsтАФcows mean heavenтАФon earth and in the Vedas, and who is their knower. The meaning of the fourth word [тАЬGop─лjanavallabhaтАЭ] is the one who sets in motion the milkmaidens, who are parts (kal─Б) of ignorance (avidy─Б), being women. Alternatively, the milkmaidens alone are complete knowledge (─Бvidy─Б), being the means to attain him. And that knowledge is an art

(kal─Б), that is, a special potency and he is the inspirer of it. The meaning of the fifth word [Sv─Бh─Б] is his M─Бy─Б. This is the drift.

Takes pleasure in him means who tastes him through praise and so on.

And also, further on (Gop─Бlat─Бpan─л Upaniс╣гad 1.14тАУ16):

┬╣тБ╡тБ╕Devotion is his worship, fixing the mind on him to the exclusion of anything either in this world or the next. That is indeed тАЬrefraining from actionтАЭ.

┬╣тБ╡тБ╣Br─Бhmaс╣Зas sacrifice in many ways to this Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa,

they have fixed themselves on this being of Govinda in many ways.

Gop─лjanavallabha has established the worlds.

Taking refuge in Sv─Бh─Б, he animates the world, his own seed.

[тАж] He means Gop─лjanavallabha. His own seed means that which has sprung from himself.

┬╣тБ╢тБ░Just as the one breath enters the body

and becomes fivefold in each one,

so also the one Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa, for the benefit of the world,

by sound exists as this five-part mantra.

[тАж] Five-part mantra means this eighteen-syllable mantra.

And also, immediately following the description of the rules for worshipping him (Gop─Бlat─Бpan─л Upaniс╣гad 1.19тАУ24):

┬╣тБ╢┬╣The one worshipable controller, all-pervading, is Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa,

who even though one, exists as many.

The wise ones who constantly worship him on his throne

attain unending happiness, not others.[^FNB000073]

┬╣тБ╢┬▓Eernal among the eternals,

conscious among the conscious, the one who fulfils the desires of many,

The wise ones who constantly worship him on his throne

attain unending perfection, not others.[^FNB000074]

┬╣тБ╢┬│For those who without selfishness are constantly

engaged in the worship of this highest abode of Viс╣гс╣Зu

he then in the form of a cowherd carefully

reveals his own abode.

┬╣тБ╢тБ┤He who in the beginning created Brahm─Б

and entrusted him with knowledge, is Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa.

Those who desire liberation should take shelter

of him who reveals his being through love.

[тАж]

┬╣тБ╢тБ╡Those who repeat this five-part mantra of Govinda,

preceded and followed by the syllable

Oс╣ВтАФ

to him he will show his own form.

One desiring liberation should therefore practise this for eternal peace.

For eternal peace, for imperishable happiness.

┬╣тБ╢тБ╢Therefore other mantras for humans have sprung

from this five-part one of Govinda,

such as the ten-syllable one.

They are practised by those who desire wealth,

such as Indra and others.

┬╣тБ╢тБ╖This Br─Бhmaс╣Зa then said: тАЬIncessantly I meditated and offered praise, and at the end of the first half of my life, he awoke. тАЬLater, when the desire to create appeared to me, he revealed the form of the future world n the letters [of the mantra]. That is, water comes from K; earth from L; fire from ─к; the moon from с╣В; from their encounter, the sun. Thus I created from the word

And later in this ┼Ъruti (Gop─Бlat─Бpan─л Upaniс╣гad 1.27тАУ28):

┬╣тБ╖┬╣By this sacrifice alone, Candradhvaja,[^FNB000077] having made himself known as free from illusion, recited the mantra with

Oс╣В at the beginning and at the end. Free from attachment he realised it.

The gods always behold the highest abode of Viс╣гс╣Зu,

like brightness spread across the sky.[^FNB000078]

Therefore, one should always practise this. And so on.

Having made known means having understood, Or else having taught others. [тАж]

Further on in the same text (Gop─Бlat─Бpan─л Upaniс╣гad 1.30тАУ33):

^(172тАУ173)About this there are songs: By practising the one mantra by the first word of which earth was manifested; by the second, water; by the third, fire; by the fourth, air, and by the fifth, space, Candradhvaja went to the imperishable supreme abode of Viс╣гс╣Зu.

By the first word of which: this refers to another eon, since the method [of creation] mentioned is different.[^FNB000079]

┬╣тБ╖тБ┤Then, completely pure and stainless,

without sorrow, without all kinds of greed and so on,

that abode, the same as the five-sectioned mantra

is V─Бsudeva, other than which there is nothing else.[^FNB000080]

┬╣тБ╣тБ╡Following the path of the ─Аgamas, which accords with the Vedas, everybody, including ┼Ъ┼лdras, may worship the gods, using the names.[^FNB000087] ┬╣тБ╣тБ╢Even women, devoted to the welfare of their husbands, are eligible for worshipping Viс╣гс╣Зu. This is the eternal revelation!

In the Agastya Saс╣Гhit─Б, explaining the king of R─Бma mantras (8.15тАУ16ab):[^FNB000088]

┬╣тБ╣тБ╖┼Ъ┼лdras who are most virtuous in conduct, righteous and serving the twiceborn; women who are faithful to their husbands; as well as other people, born of regular or irregular unions, including outcastes: all are eligible here.

┬╣тБ╣тБ╕When giving the mantra, the guru should consider Siddha, S─Бdhya and so on; whether or not the mantra is Related or Unrelated; Young or Mature; ┬╣тБ╣тБ╣Male, Female or Neuter; the Junction of the signs and the lunar mansions; the time of its being Asleep and Awake; as well as if it is a Debtor or Creditor, etc.[^FNB000089]

[тАж] Etc. refers to determining the Astrological sign. Thus there are eight ways of determining its qualities.

The Determination of Siddha, S─Бdhya and so on

┬▓тБ░тБ░Five lines should first be drawn from east to west and then from south to north. This makes a diagram of four times four squares.

Even though this knowledge of Siddha, S─Бdhya and so on, like the way of showing Mudr─Бs, cannot be fully understood without learning it from a guru, the author still gives a sense of the meaning here. vertical[^FNB000091] and face the east and west. Then one should draw five lines from the south to the north, facing south and north, on top of the vertical lines. These lines should be horizontal, for the purpose of creating equal squares. Thus one forms a diagram of four times four squares.

Now, by four squares one [large] square is formed. These four [large] squares should be understood as the primary [squares]. Then, since each such square has four squares within, there are sixteen squares [all in all]. The meaning is that one arrives at a rectangular diagram with this form. It is called a diagram (maс╣Зс╕Нala), just as an initiation diagram, even though it does not have the [usual circular] shape of such a diagram, being rectangular.

┬▓тБ░┬╣The wise one should then draw the letters of the alphabet, one after another, in the first, third, eleventh, ninth, second, fourth, twelfth, tenth, sixth, eighth, sixteenth, fourteenth, fifth, seventh, fifteenth and thirteenth squares.[^FNB000092]

The author now explains what one is to do in this diagram. The letters of the alphabet: the fifty letters beginning with A and ending with Kс╣гa. Or else, the forty-nine letters, leaving out Kс╣гa, since that is a combination of K and с╣вa. [тАж] These letters should be drawn in order in the first, third, and so on squares, in the order of A, ─А and so on. [тАж] In the thirteenth square, the sixteenth letter from A should be drawn, that is с╕д. Then one should start again in the first square with K and continue writing until the end of the alphabet.

This is also stated in the book Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhaparicary─Б of Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зadeva ─Аc─Бrya (1.14): тАЬIn the first, third, eleventh, ninth, second, fourth, twelfth, tenth, sixth, eighth, sixteenth, fourteenth, fifth, seventh, fifteenth and thirteenth should the letters be placed, one after the other.тАЭ[^FNB000093]

┬▓тБ░┬▓From the letter of the birth lunar mansion one should look up the first letter of the mantra, first in one rectangle of four squares. ┬▓тБ░┬│Then the discerning ones should assign Siddha, S─Бdhya, Susiddha and Ari, one after the other, beginning with [the square with] the letter of the birth lunar mansion and towards the left.[^FNB000094]

The first letter of the name of the disciple, conforming to the lunar mansion during which he was born. Here in the middle lands and elsewhere as well, the first letter of the name usually conforms to the birth lunar man-

Now, having given the opinion of the ┼Ъ─Бrad─Бtilaka, the author gives the opinion of ┼Ъr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зadeva ─Аc─Бrya beginning with тАЬAnd sometimesтАЭ.[^FNB000097] [тАж] One should gradually count from the first letter of the name of the practitioner, the disciple, until one arrives at the first letter of the mantra. The meaning is that one arrives at knowledge of Siddha and so on by going left or counterclockwise from the first letter of the practitionerтАЩs name. Siddha is where the first letter of the mantra is found; S─Бdhya in the second square; Susiddha in the third and Ari in the fourth. Therefore it was said that one should go left. This is the drift.[^FNB000098]

┬▓тБ░тБ┤A Siddha [mantra] is perfected in time, S─Бdhya by recitations and fire sacrifices, Susiddha simply by accepting it. Ari cuts at the root.[^FNB000099]

And then, by counting, when one at the first letter of the mantra arrives at the place of Siddha, etc., one learns what fruit the mantra will bring. This the author explains in verses204тАУ208. Simply by accepting it means that it brings perfection immediately.

┬▓тБ░тБ╡Siddha-siddha [brings perfection] by the prescribed amount of recitations; Siddha-s─Бdhya by the double; Siddha-susiddha by half; Siddha-ari destroys oneтАЩs kinsmen. ┬▓тБ░тБ╢S─Бdhya-siddha by twice the amount; S─Бdhya-s─Бdhya is useless; S─Бdhya-susiddha by thrice the amount;[^FNB000100] S─Бdhya-ari kills oneтАЩs relatives. ┬▓тБ░тБ╖Susiddha-siddha by half of the recitations; Susiddha-s─Бdhya by three times the amount; Susiddha-susiddha by just accepting it; Susiddha-ari is killer of oneтАЩs kinsmen. ┬▓тБ░тБ╕Ari-siddha kills oneтАЩs sons; Ari-s─Бdhya the daughters; Ari-susiddha the wife, Ari-ari the practitioner.[^FNB000101]

Mantras That Are an Exception to This

Also in the Tantra:[^FNB000102]

┬▓тБ░тБ╣One should not determine Siddha and so on for mantras of Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гha, S┼лrya, Var─Бha, the Pr─Бs─Бda-root mantra,[^FNB000103] Oс╣Г or Vedic mantras. ┬▓┬╣тБ░One should also not determine Siddha and so on if it was attained in a dream, given by a woman, if it is a M─Бl─Б-mantra,[^FNB000104] or has one or three syllables.

To this means to this determination of Siddha and so on.

┬▓┬╣┬╣Whether the mantra is Related or Unrelated, and so on, should be learned from other ─Аgamas.[^FNB000105] Fearing to enlarge the book too much, and since it is unnecessary, it is not given here. ┬▓┬╣┬▓That should never be determined for mantras that have the same power as blessed Lord Gop─Бla, who exhibits all kinds of majesty.

┬▓┬▓тБ┤Thus, in other mantras than this, there are faults, also the latter ones. For this reason, ten Tantric methods of purifying mantras are given.

Thus, following the statements of the Sammohana Tantra and other texts. In other: in mantras other than the Gop─Бla mantra. The latter ones: the faults of being Cut, and so on, that are different from the faults learned through Siddha, etc. For this reason: for purifying such faults for those who may practise other mantras. The implied meaning is that this also announces the further glories of the mantra of Lord Gop─Бla. Tantric: described in the ─Аgama scriptures.

рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпреЛрджреНрджреЗрд╢рдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдг рддрдерд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдПрддрджреН рдЙрджреАрд░рд┐рддрдореН реереирейрекрее

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрдЧреЛрдкрд╛рд▓рднрдЯреНрдЯрд╡рд┐рд▓рд┐рдЦрд┐рддреЗ1041 рднрдЧрд╡рджреН1042рднрдХреНрддрд┐рд╡рд┐рд▓рд╛рд╕реЗ рдЧреМрд░рд╡реЛ рдирд╛рдо рдкреНрд░рдердореЛ рд╡рд┐рд▓рд╛рд╕рдГ реерезрее

Broo

the mantra is called Offering libations. ┬▓┬│┬│Prefixing the mantra with

Oс╣В HR─кс╣В ┼ЪR─кс╣В is kindling. To keep the mantra one recites secret is Concealing.

[тАж]

┬▓┬│тБ┤Because of the strength of Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa mantras, there is no consideration of purification for them. Still, this has been mentioned in a very general way.

Thus ends the first chapter of the Bhagavadbhaktivil─Бsa written by Gop─Бla Bhaс╣нс╣нa, called тАЬOn the GuruтАЭ.
